{"Quotes": "\"Zn-modified zeolites are effective catalysts for light alkanes aromatization [14]. The enhanced selectivity of alkane conversion (ethane [57] and propane [8,9]) towards aromatics is attributed to dehydrogenation ability of the loaded zinc species.\"\n\n\"It has been claimed [2,3] that strong Lewis sites, which are generated by zinc, change the mechanism of alkane activation and transformation from the beta scission to a dehydrogenation step.\"\n\n\"For Zn/H-BEA, the kinetic parameters of H/D exchange change dramatically. The rate constants kSiOHAl are at least two orders of magnitude higher. The activation energy of 86-88 kJ mol-1 is rather low. The exchange proceeds with a notable rate at temperatures at least 100 K lower compared to that on H-BEA.\"\n\n\"The promotion may consist of involvement of Zn-alkyl species in the exchange. They can be formed either on ZnO clusters or Zn2+ cations, located on neighbor or remote SiO()Al groups.\"\n\n\"Kazansky et al. [12–14] demonstrated the formation of strong adsorption complexes between small alkanes and Zn2+ cations by IR spectroscopy. They claimed that the activation of the alkane molecules in zeolite occurred on Zn2+ cations.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly Zn-modified zeolites, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations:\n\n1. Composition:\n   - Zinc loading enhances selectivity towards aromatics due to its dehydrogenation ability.\n   - Strong Lewis sites generated by zinc change the mechanism of alkane activation from beta scission to dehydrogenation.\n\n2. Structure:\n   - Zinc can be present as ZnO clusters or Zn2+ cations located on SiO()Al groups in the zeolite framework.\n   - Zn2+ cations form strong adsorption complexes with small alkanes, facilitating their activation.\n\n3. Reaction conditions:\n   - Zn-modified zeolites allow for lower reaction temperatures, at least 100 K lower than unmodified zeolites.\n\n4. Efficiency:\n   - Rate constants for Zn/H-BEA are at least two orders of magnitude higher than for H-BEA.\n   - Activation energy is significantly lower (86-88 kJ/mol for Zn/H-BEA vs. 138 kJ/mol for H-BEA).\n\n5. Reaction mechanism:\n   - Zn-alkyl species are involved as intermediates in the reaction mechanism.\n   - The activation of alkane molecules occurs on Zn2+ cations.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of metal-modified zeolites by allowing for more selective, efficient, and energy-saving processes in alkane transformations such as aromatization, dehydrogenation, and H/D exchange reactions.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂（特别是锌改性沸石）的组成、结构和反应条件显著影响烷烃转化的机理和效率：\n\n1. 组成：\n   - 锌负载增强了对芳烃的选择性，这归因于其脱氢能力。\n   - 锌产生的强Lewis酸位将烷烃活化机理从β裂解改变为脱氢。\n\n2. 结构：\n   - 锌可以以ZnO簇或位于沸石骨架SiO()Al基团上的Zn2+阳离子形式存在。\n   - Zn2+阳离子与小分子烷烃形成强吸附络合物，促进其活化。\n\n3. 反应条件：\n   - 锌改性沸石允许在更低的反应温度下进行，比未改性沸石至少低100 K。\n\n4. 效率：\n   - Zn/H-BEA的反应速率常数至少比H-BEA高两个数量级。\n   - 活化能显著降低（Zn/H-BEA为86-88 kJ/mol，而H-BEA为138 kJ/mol）。\n\n5. 反应机理：\n   - Zn-烷基物种作为中间体参与反应机理。\n   - 烷烃分子的活化发生在Zn2+阳离子上。\n\n这些因素通过允许在烷烃转化（如芳构化、脱氢和H/D交换反应）过程中实现更具选择性、更高效和更节能的过程，提高了金属改性沸石的工业重要性。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2007.11.002"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"In general, in propane ODH catalysts made of Voxide supported on silica are more selective than those made with the alumina support, and the latter are more selective than those supported on titania, mainly because of the lower extent of parallel propane combustion, especially at low vanadia loading\"\n\n[2] \"The reduction and catalytic properties of active VOx domains can be significantly affected by the formation of binary dispersed structures. For example, VOx-CrOx and VOx-MoOx mixed structures lead to a higher propane ODH rate and selectivity than VOx domains present at similar surface densities on pure Al2O3 supports\"\n\n[3] \"The activation of the ethane CH bond proceeds through the formation of alkoxides, which decompose to ethylene and a surface OH group or are oxidized to surface-bound oxygenates (acetaldehyde).\"\n\n[4] \"A key factor in the design of efficient catalysts for alkane ODH is the isolation of active sites. Therefore, the isomorphous substitution of active metal species, e.g., vanadium, into microporous and mesoporous materials is an attractive strategy for designing new catalysts for this reaction\"\n\n[5] \"In the case of VCoAPO-18, the presence of both acid sites (related to the presence of Co2+ cations) and redox sites (related to the presence of V5+/4+ and Co3+/2+) seems to be an important factor in achieving high selectivities to ethylene during the ODH of ethane\"\n\n[6] \"The catalytic activity of vanadium oxide catalysts increases with the V2O5 loading, while rates per V-atom reach a maximum on VOx domains of intermediate size, providing a balance between the activity of surface VOx species and their accessibility to reactants.\"\n\n[7] \"For both propane and ethane, reactivity data for catalysts made of supported vanadium oxide are consistent both with kinetically relevant steps involving the dissociation of CH bonds (methylenic C atom in propane) and with a Mars-van Krevelen redox mechanism involving lattice oxygen in CH bond activation.\"\n\n[8] \"One of the best performing catalysts in propane ODH is the VOx-SBA-15 system, prepared by an alcoholic impregnation method, in which the introduction of V species onto the inner walls of SBA-15 provides a system with a large concentration of accessible, isolated and structurally well-defined active sites.\"\n\n[9] \"The selectivity to propylene formation is affected by surface reduction: the higher the surface reduction, the higher the selectivity\"\n\n[10] \"Additives (e.g., P, K, Ca, Ni, Cr, Nb, Mg, Au, Zn and Mo), sometimes added in relevant amount with respect to V, modify acidbasic and redox properties of supported vanadium oxide\"\n\n[11] \"Examples include V-containing high-surface siliceous materials, such as MCM-41, MCM-48 or SBA-15. In these systems, the catalytic activity of vanadium is strongly influenced by its local environment and the co-existence of acid sites in the host material.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in oxidative dehydrogenation (ODH) processes:\n\n1. Catalyst composition:\n   - Support material affects selectivity: silica > alumina > titania for propane ODH.\n   - V2O5 loading impacts catalytic activity, with optimal performance at intermediate loadings.\n   - Binary dispersed structures (e.g., VOx-CrOx, VOx-MoOx) can enhance ODH rate and selectivity.\n   - Additives (P, K, Ca, Ni, Cr, Nb, Mg, Au, Zn, Mo) modify acid-base and redox properties.\n\n2. Catalyst structure:\n   - Isolation of active sites is crucial for efficient ODH catalysts.\n   - Isomorphous substitution of active metals into microporous and mesoporous materials (e.g., MCM-41, MCM-48, SBA-15) is an effective design strategy.\n   - VOx-SBA-15 system provides high concentration of accessible, isolated, and well-defined active sites.\n\n3. Reaction mechanism:\n   - Follows Mars-van Krevelen redox mechanism involving lattice oxygen in C-H bond activation.\n   - Ethane ODH proceeds through alkoxide formation, decomposing to ethylene or oxidizing to oxygenates.\n\n4. {"Quotes": "[1] \"All catalysts used industrially for the production of maleic anhydride from butane are PVO-based systems.\"\n\n[2] \"The vanadyl pyrophosphate catalyst, due to its particular crystalline structure, shows a singular ability to control its oxidizing power.\"\n\n[3] \"The best selectivity is achieved when desorption of less selective intermediates along the reaction coordinate is avoided because the olefin reactions are less selective on a highly active butane (VO)2P2O7 catalyst.\"\n\n[4] \"The availability of oxygen to the surface is critical in avoiding desorption of less selective olefins. Thus it would appear that major selectivity gains could be achieved if more oxygen could be channeled to the active site.\"\n\n[5] \"A central role in the modification of surface reactivity is adsorption of organic molecules and oxygen species. The mobility of these species under steady-state conditions of reaction is another characteristic of the vanadyl pyrophosphate catalyst in n-butane oxidation\"\n\n[6] \"The vanadium phosphorus oxide system is characterized by facile formation and interconversion of a number of crystalline V(IV) and V(V) phases, and this has led to some confusion in the literature as to the nature of the active phase.\"\n\n[7] \"Kinetics data agree that the hydrocarbon activation is the first step in n-butane oxidation.\"\n\n[8] \"The TAP results suggest that the selectivity of the butane oxidation reaction is influenced by the concentration of these species at the initial butane adsorption site.\"\n\n[9] \"Activation of the alkane hydrocarbon is a further important aspect of this reaction because of its mechanistic relevance in the study of other heterogeneous reactions for functionalization of alkanes\"\n\n[10] \"A very specific surface structure is needed, and it would seem that the binding of intermediates until product is formed (single-site process) is essential to high selectivities.\"\n\n[11] \"For example, the use of an organic solvent during preparation as opposed to an aqueous system results in differing degrees of crystallinity and defect structure of the resulting active phase.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly vanadium phosphorus oxide (VPO) catalysts, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in processes like oxidative dehydrogenation and n-butane oxidation to maleic anhydride. Key factors include:\n\n1. Catalyst composition: VPO catalysts contain both V(IV) and V(V) phases, with the optimal ratio depending on reaction conditions.\n\n2. Crystal structure: The vanadyl pyrophosphate ((VO)2P2O7) phase is considered the active phase. Its unique crystalline structure allows precise control of oxidizing power, which is crucial for selectivity.\n\n3. Surface properties: The concentration and type of oxygen species on the surface, as well as the adsorption of organic molecules, play a crucial role in determining catalyst activity and selectivity.\n\n4. Reaction conditions: Oxygen availability at the surface is critical. Improving oxygen channeling to active sites could potentially increase selectivity.\n\n5. Preparation method: The use of organic solvents versus aqueous systems during synthesis affects the crystallinity and defect structure of the active phase.\n\n6. Redox properties: The ability of the catalyst to undergo controlled reduction and reoxidation is key to its selectivity.\n\n7. Intermediate binding: A specific surface structure that binds intermediates until product formation (single-site process) is essential for high selectivities.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of VPO catalysts for n-butane oxidation. Their unique ability to selectively activate and transform alkanes without releasing intermediates allows for high selectivity to maleic anhydride, which has not been matched by other catalytic systems.\n\nWhile the focus is on VPO catalysts for butane oxidation, the principles discussed regarding controlled redox properties, oxygen mobility, and surface reactivity are relevant to other metal-based catalysts for alkane transformations. However, specific mechanisms and efficiency factors may differ for other systems such as supported vanadium oxides or metal-exchanged zeolites used in oxidative dehydrogenation or other zeolite-catalyzed reactions.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂的组成、结构和反应条件，特别是钒磷氧化物（VPO）催化剂，显著影响烷烃转化过程中的机理和效率，如氧化脱氢过程和正丁烷氧化制顺丁烯二酸酐。关键因素包括：\n\n1. 催化剂组成：VPO催化剂含有V(IV)和V(V)相，最佳比例取决于反应条件。\n\n2. 晶体结构：焦磷酸钒酰((VO)2P2O7)被认为是活性相。其独特的晶体结构允许精确控制氧化能力，这对选择性至关重要。\n\n3. 表面性质：表面氧物种的浓度和类型，以及有机分子的吸附，在决定催化剂活性和选择性方面起着关键作用。\n\n4. 反应条件：表面氧的可用性至关重要。改善氧气向活性位点的输送可能会增加选择性。\n\n5. 制备方法：在合成过程中使用有机溶剂与水系统会影响活性相的结晶度和缺陷结构。\n\n6. 氧化还原性质：催化剂进行可控还原和再氧化的能力是其选择性的关键。\n\n7. 中间体结合：能够结合中间体直至产物形成（单点过程）的特定表面结构对于获得高选择性至关重要。\n\n这些因素造就了VPO催化剂在正丁烷氧化中的工业重要性。它们独特的能力可以选择性地活化和转化烷烃而不释放中间体，从而对顺丁烯二酸酐有高选择性，这是其他催化系统所无法匹敌的。\n\n虽然重点关注用于丁烷氧化的VPO催化剂，但关于控制氧化还原性质、氧移动性和表面反应性的讨论原则也适用于其他用于烷烃转化的金属基催化剂。然而，对于其他系统，如用于氧化脱氢或其他沸石催化反应的负载型钒氧化物或金属交换沸石，具体机理和影响效率的因素可能会有所不同。", "Doi": "10.1021/cr00083a003"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Zn- or Ga-modified zeolites effectively catalyze the conversion of light alkanes to aromatics with high selectivity.\"\n\n[2] \"The role of the metal species and acid sites of a zeolite in the enhancement of light alkane conversion to aromatics remains a subject of intense controversy, even after significant emphasis and numerous publications.\"\n\n[3] \"There is agreement on the bifunctional nature of these catalysts, where the metal species are responsible for the dehydrogenation of alkanes, while the Brnsted acid sites are involved in the oligomerization and cyclization of olefins.\"\n\n[4] \"When zeolites are modified with Zn, the picture of hydrogen exchange changes. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The dehydroaromatization of methane to benzene has been investigated over a 2 wt% Mo/ZSM-5 catalyst in the absence of an added oxidant.\"\n\n[2] \"Under typical CH4 reaction conditions at 700C, 60–80% of the original Mo6+ ions are reduced to form Mo2C, with the remaining Mo occurring primarily as Mo4+ and traces of Mo5+ ions.\"\n\n[3] \"Exposure of a 2 wt% Mo/ZSM-5 catalyst to CH4 or to CH4/H2 at 700C causes reduction of Mo ions to Mo2C, rather than to metallic Mo.\"\n\n[4] \"Since preformation of Mo2C on the catalyst, without coke deposition, does not completely eliminate the induction period, it is believed that the clean surface of Mo2C may be too reactive to form higher hydrocarbons and, thus, that a coke-modified Mo2C surface may be the actual active species in the formation of ethylene as the reaction intermediate.\"\n\n[5] \"The presence of a certain concentration of acid sites in Mo/ZSM-5 catalysts is thus necessary to achieve a high benzene selectivity and a high methane conversion, since the formation of aromatics is thermodynamically favored\"\n\n[6] \"During preparation and/or pretreatment of the catalyst, a portion of the Mo ions diffuses into the channels of the zeolite. The amount of Mo ions within the channels depends on the temperature, time, and atmosphere of calcination.\"\n\n[7] \"It appears that the dispersion of molybdenum oxide species on the surface of ZSM-5 may occur slowly and/or may be restricted to a short distance.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly Mo/ZSM-5, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, especially in the dehydroaromatization of methane to benzene. Key factors include:\n\n1. Catalyst composition: 2 wt% Mo loading on ZSM-5 zeolite support is effective for methane conversion to benzene.\n\n2. Catalyst structure: Mo species are initially present on the external surface of ZSM-5 and partially diffuse into the zeolite channels during preparation and pretreatment. The distribution of Mo affects catalyst performance.\n\n3. Reaction conditions: High temperature (700°C) and the absence of added oxidants are critical. These conditions promote the reduction of Mo6+ to Mo2C, which is the active species for methane activation.\n\n4. The formation of Mo2C corresponds to the initial activation period for benzene production.\n\n5. Surface modification: A coke-modified Mo2C surface is believed to be the actual active species for forming ethylene as a reaction intermediate, as the clean Mo2C surface may be too reactive.\n\n6. Acid sites: The presence of acid sites in the zeolite is necessary for high benzene selectivity and methane conversion, as they promote the formation of aromatics.\n\n7. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Supported vanadium oxide in heterogeneous catalysis: elucidating the structureactivity relationship with spectroscopy\"\n\n[2] \"Reactivity in the confined spaces of zeolites: the interplay between spectroscopy and theory to develop structureactivity relationships for catalysis\"\n\n[3] \"Binuclear sites are argued to account for the enhanced activity of oxygenated gallium-exchanged high-silica zeolites in alkane dehydrogenation.\"\n\n[4] \"These sites, however, tend to decompose via water desorption upon the catalytic reaction resulting in less reactive reduced Ga+ ions.\"\n\n[5] \"As per predictions from the quantum-chemical calculations, the experimental results show that the high alkane dehydrogenation activity can be maintained by in situ hydrolysis of the reduced extraframework Ga species.\"\n\n[6] \"Clearly, co-feeding of water leads to a substantial increase of the propane conversion. The conversion passes a maximum at pH2O of 0.3 kPa.\"\n\n[7] \"The promoting effect of water is due to the formation of reactive partly hydrolyzed gallium species such as [HGaOGaOH]2+ and [HGa(OH)2GaH]2+ discussed above.\"\n\n[8] \"Addition of water to the hydrocarbon feed increases significantly the dehydrogenation activity. The main product remains propylene although with increasing water content, formation of the products of propane cracking (methane and ethylene) is observed.\"\n\n[9] \"Formation of less stable intermediate products in the catalytic cycle facilitates the regeneration of the active site. Indeed, moderate barriers are calculated for H2 recombination in the catalytic cycle involving [HGa(OH)(O)Ga]2+ species.\"\n\n[10] \"Although earlier isolated mononuclear GaO+ have been proposed as the active sites in Ga-containing high-silica zeolites, the present results indicate that such species should oligomerize in the microporous space, independent of the Al distribution.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in processes such as oxidative dehydrogenation and zeolite-catalyzed reactions:\n\n1. Structure-activity relationships: For supported vanadium oxides and zeolites, understanding the structure-activity relationship is crucial for elucidating catalytic behavior in heterogeneous catalysis.\n\n2. Confined spaces in zeolites: The reactivity in zeolites is greatly affected by their confined spaces, with spectroscopy and theory interplaying to develop structure-activity relationships.\n\n3. Binuclear sites: In gallium-exchanged high-silica zeolites, binuclear sites are believed to enhance activity in alkane dehydrogenation, rather than isolated mononuclear GaO+ species.\n\n4. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Supported vanadium oxide catalysts, containing surface vanadia species on oxide supports, are extensively employed as catalysts for many hydrocarbon oxidation reactions.\"\n\n[2] \"The molecular structures of these surface vanadia species are tentatively thought to consist of a terminal V=O bond and three bridging V-O-support bonds for the isolated species, and a terminal V=O bond with one bridging V-O-support and two bridging V-O-V bonds for the polymerized species.\"\n\n[3] \"The bridging V-O-support bond appears to be associated with the critical oxygen required for hydrocarbon oxidation reactions since changing the specific oxide support dramatically affects the TOF: approximately four orders of magnitude for methanol oxidation to formaldehyde and two-orders of magnitude for butane oxidation to maleic anhydride.\"\n\n[4] \"The general trend appears to be CeOz>ZrO2 TiO2>NbzOs>A12Os>SiO2, which inversely correlates with the Sanderson electronegativity of the oxide support cations.\"\n\n[5] \"As a result of these physical and chemical characteristics, supported vanadia catalysts tend to be among the most active and selective supported metal oxide catalysts for hydrocarbon oxidation reactions.\"\n\n[6] \"The oxidative dehydrogenation of propane to propylene over V2O5/Nb2O5 was not dependent on the concentration of the bridging V-O-V bonds\"\n\n[7] \"Oxidation reactions requiring only one surface vanadia sites are generally not sensitive to the surface vanadia coverage and the presence of noninteracting metal oxide additives. Oxidation reactions requiring multiple surface vanadia sites are very sensitive to surface vanadia coverage and the presence of noninteracting metal oxide additives.\"\n\n[8] \"The addition of surface niobia is especially informative since it has a minimal effect on the surface vanadia structure, see Section 5.6 above, and its presence primarily increases the number of adjacent surface metal oxide sites for the surface vanadia species.\"\n\n[9] \"Interacting additives affect all hydrocarbon oxidation reactions since they directly alter the structure and reactivity of the surface vanadia sites.\"\n\n[10] \"Acidic and basic additives also influence the selectivity of hydrocarbon oxidation reactions, but the effect appears to be reaction specific and cannot be generalized with the limited data currently available.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of supported vanadium oxide catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in oxidative dehydrogenation processes. Key factors contributing to their industrial significance include:\n\n1. Support material: The choice of oxide support (e.g., CeO2, ZrO2, TiO2, Nb2O5, Al2O3, SiO2) dramatically affects catalyst performance. The bridging V-O-support bond is critical, as it can change the turnover frequency (TOF) for hydrocarbon oxidation reactions by up to four orders of magnitude.\n\n2. Surface structure: Surface vanadia species typically consist of isolated species with a terminal V=O bond and three bridging V-O-support bonds, or polymerized species with a terminal V=O bond, one V-O-support bond, and two V-O-V bonds.\n\n3. Support electronegativity: The reactivity trend (CeO2 > ZrO2 > TiO2 > Nb2O5 > Al2O3 > SiO2) inversely correlates with the Sanderson electronegativity of the oxide support cations, affecting the basicity of the bridging oxygens.\n\n4. Surface coverage and additives: The sensitivity to surface vanadia coverage and non-interacting metal oxide additives depends on whether the reaction requires single or multiple surface vanadia sites. For example, the oxidative dehydrogenation of propane to propylene over V2O5/Nb2O5 was not dependent on the concentration of bridging V-O-V bonds.\n\n5. Interacting additives: These directly alter the structure and reactivity of surface vanadia sites, affecting all hydrocarbon oxidation reactions.\n\n6. Acidic and basic additives: These influence the selectivity of hydrocarbon oxidation reactions, though their effects are reaction-specific and not yet fully understood.\n\nThese factors allow for the tuning of catalyst properties to optimize performance in specific alkane transformation processes, contributing to the industrial significance of supported vanadium oxide catalysts. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Ga/H-ZSM-5 catalysts are most active and selective for the aromatisation of propane [1]. It is widely accepted that their activity and selectivity result from their bifunctional properties, whereby gallium species are responsible for their dehydrogenation-hydrogenation activity and the Brönsted acid sites of the zeolite provide the centres necessary for chain growth.\"\n\n[2] \"Recently, it was shown that dual active sites are responsible for the activation of propane on Ga/H-ZSM-5 [2-4]. These dual active sites consist of highly dispersed (Ga3+, O2-) ions pairs, acting in synergy with neighbouring Brönsted sites which initially activate propane as a protonated pseudo-cyclopropane species.\"\n\n[3] \"Changes in the propane aromatisation activity and selectivity of these catalysts as a function of the number of reaction (reducing conditions)-regeneration (oxidative conditions) cycles sustained were explained by the migration of gallium species in and out of the zeolite intracrystalline void space [5] as substantiated by detailed catalyst characterisation [6].\"\n\n[4] \"Hydrogen treatment increases activity and selectivity to aromatics while decreasing the formation of methane. Subsequent oxygen treatment enhances further the activity and aromatics selectivity and has little effect on methane selectivity.\"\n\n[5] \"These improvements of catalytic performance are explained by gallium migration in reducing conditions. The concentration of highly dispersed gallium species is thereby enhanced. These species, in association with Brønsted centers, were reported previously to constitute the dual catalytic sites responsible for alkane activation.\"\n\n[6] \"Several authors have also reported the inhibitory effect of hydrogen on propane transformation over Zn/H-ZSM-5 [24] and Ga/H-ZSM-5 catalysts [25]. A possible explanation is that the limiting step of the propane dehydrogenation is the removal of hydrogen [26].\"\n\n[7] \"H2-O2 pretreatment thus appear to be a promising way to preactivate and stabilise Ga-modified aromatisation catalysts in commercial operation.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly Ga/H-ZSM-5, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, especially in processes such as propane aromatization. Key factors include:\n\n1. Composition: The bifunctional nature of Ga/H-ZSM-5 catalysts, with gallium species responsible for dehydrogenation-hydrogenation activity and Brönsted acid sites from the zeolite enabling chain growth, is crucial for their high activity and selectivity.\n\n2. Structure: Dual active sites consisting of highly dispersed (Ga3+, O2-) ion pairs working synergistically with neighboring Brönsted sites are responsible for propane activation. The dispersion of gallium species within the zeolite structure is vital for catalyst performance.\n\n3. Reaction conditions:\n   a) Reducing conditions (H2 treatment) increase gallium dispersion, leading to higher activity and aromatics selectivity while reducing methane formation.\n   b) Oxidative conditions (O2 treatment) following H2 treatment further boost activity and aromatics selectivity without affecting methane selectivity.\n   c) Hydrogen can have an inhibitory effect on propane transformation, possibly due to its impact on the rate-limiting step of propane dehydrogenation.\n\n4. Catalyst activation: H2-O2 pretreatment cycles dramatically improve catalytic performance by optimizing gallium dispersion and oxidation state. This pretreatment eliminates the induction period and could be industrially significant for preactivating and stabilizing catalysts before use in aromatization units.\n\n5. Reaction-regeneration cycles: The migration of gallium species in and out of the zeolite intracrystalline void space during reaction (reducing) and regeneration (oxidative) cycles affects catalyst performance over time.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of these catalysts by enhancing their activity, selectivity, and stability in alkane transformation processes, particularly in propane aromatization. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Previous studies have shown that supported vanadia is the most active and selective simple metal oxide for alkane ODH, because its reducible nature leads to the rapid redox cycles required for a catalytic turnover (15).\"\n\n[2] \"UVvisible spectroscopy suggests that V5+ is present in distorted tetrahedrally coordinated species at low vanadia surface densities and that some of these tetrahedrally coordinated cations remain at higher surface densities, coexisting with an increasing fraction of V5+ present in distorted tetragonal pyramidal coordination, similar to that present in V2O5 (25).\"\n\n[3] \"For both ethane and propane reactants, these apparent turnover rates reach a maximum at intermediate vanadia surface densities. The maximum rate is reached at a surface VOx density of 8 V/nm2 for both reactants, and this maximum rate is about four times greater than that obtained on the VOx/Al2O3 sample with the lowest surface density (1.4 V/nm2).\"\n\n[4] \"Ethane ODH at zero conversion is 75% selective to ethene and insensitive to vanadia surface density, while initial propene selectivities during propane ODH approach 90% at low vanadia surface densities, but decrease with increasing vanadia surface density.\"\n\n[5] \"Therefore, the highest olefin yields are obtained on catalysts containing isolated monovanadates and operated at the highest possible reaction temperature consistent with the avoidance of homogeneous reactions.\"\n\n[6] \"VOx/Al2O3 catalysts were prepared by incipient wetness impregnation of fumed γ-alumina (Degussa, AG, 100 m2/g) with an aqueous solution of ammonium metavanadate (99%, Aldrich, Inc.) and oxalic acid (Mallinckrodt analytical grade) in a 1 : 2 weight ratio (12) with a pH of 2.\"\n\n[7] \"Reaction rate and selectivity data were measured in a packed-bed flow reactor with plug-flow hydrodynamics (24). VOx/Al2O3 catalysts (0.010.3 g) were diluted with quartz granules (180- to 355-m diameter, 0.010.3 g) in order to prevent bed temperature gradients.\"\n\n[8] \"Ethane ODH reactions were examined at 663743 K, while the faster propane ODH reactions were examined at lower temperatures (603663 K).\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly supported vanadium oxides, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in oxidative dehydrogenation (ODH) processes:\n\n1. Composition: VOx/Al2O3 catalysts are prepared by impregnating γ-alumina with ammonium metavanadate and oxalic acid solutions. The vanadia surface density greatly affects catalyst performance.\n\n2. Structure: At low surface densities, V5+ is present in distorted tetrahedrally coordinated species. As density increases, these coexist with an increasing fraction of V5+ in distorted tetragonal pyramidal coordination, similar to V2O5. The catalyst structure evolves from isolated monovanadates to polyvanadates and eventually V2O5 crystallites as surface density increases.\n\n3. Reaction conditions: \n   - Temperature: Ethane ODH is conducted at 663-743 K, while propane ODH occurs at 603-663 K. Higher temperatures generally increase alkene selectivity.\n   - Reactor design: A packed-bed flow reactor with plug-flow hydrodynamics is used, with catalyst dilution to prevent temperature gradients.\n\n4. Catalytic performance:\n   - Activity: Turnover rates for both ethane and propane ODH reach a maximum at intermediate vanadia surface densities (8 V/nm2), about four times higher than at the lowest density (1.4 V/nm2).\n   - Selectivity: Initial ethene selectivity is about 75% and relatively independent of surface density. Propene selectivity can reach 90% at low surface densities but decreases with increasing density.\n\n5. Industrial significance: The highest olefin yields are obtained on catalysts containing isolated monovanadates operated at the highest possible reaction temperature that avoids homogeneous reactions. This insight can guide the design of more efficient industrial catalysts for alkane ODH processes.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial importance of supported vanadium oxide catalysts for alkane ODH by allowing for the optimization of catalyst composition, structure, and reaction conditions to maximize desired product yields while minimizing unwanted side reactions.\n\nThe study does not provide information about metal-exchanged zeolites or zeolite-catalyzed reactions, so that part of the question cannot be addressed based on the given literature.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂的组成、结构和反应条件，特别是负载型钒氧化物，显著影响烷烃在氧化脱氢（ODH）过程中的转化机理和效率：\n\n1. 组成：VOx/Al2O3催化剂是通过将γ-氧化铝浸渍于偏钒酸铵和草酸溶液中制备的。钒的表面密度极大地影响催化剂的性能。\n\n2. 结构：在低表面密度下，V5+以扭曲的四面体配位形式存在。随着密度增加，这些物种与越来越多的扭曲四方锥配位的V5+共存，类似于V2O5。随着表面密度增加，催化剂结构从孤立的单钒酸盐演变为多钒酸盐，最终形成V2O5晶体。\n\n3. 反应条件：\n   - 温度：乙烷ODH在663-743 K下进行，而丙烷ODH在603-663 K下进行。较高的温度通常会增加烯烃的选择性。\n   - 反应器设计：使用具有塞流流体动力学的填充床流动反应器，并稀释催化剂以防止温度梯度。\n\n4. 催化性能：\n   - 活性：乙烷和丙烷ODH的转化率在中等钒表面密度（8 V/nm2）时达到最大值，约为最低密度（1.4 V/nm2）时的四倍。\n   - 选择性：初始乙烯选择性约为75%，与表面密度关系不大。丙烯选择性在低表面密度时可达90%，但随着密度增加而下降。\n\n5. 工业意义：在含有孤立单钒酸盐的催化剂上，在避免均相反应的最高可能反应温度下操作，可获得最高的烯烃产率。这一见解可以指导更高效的工业催化剂设计，用于烷烃ODH过程。\n\n这些因素通过允许优化催化剂组成、结构和反应条件以最大化所需产品产率，同时最小化不需要的副反应，从而为烷烃ODH的支持钒氧化物催化剂的工业重要性做出贡献。\n\n该研究没有提供关于金属交换沸石或沸石催化反应的信息，因此无法根据给定的文献回答问题的这一部分。", "Doi": "10.1006/jcat.2002.3570"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Isolated molybdate species supported on silica are reported to have the highest specific activity and selectivity for the direct oxidation of methane to formaldehyde.\"\n\n[2] \"On the basis of evidence from extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) and Raman spectroscopy, the Mo atoms in this catalyst are present as isolated, pentacoordinated molybdate species containing a single MoO bond.\"\n\n[3] \"It is proposed that peroxides are produced by the reaction of O2 with a small concentration of reduced molybdate species and that the reaction of CH4 with these peroxide species leads to the formation of formaldehyde.\"\n\n[4] \"Low concentrations of H2O were observed to enhance the activity of MoOx/SiO2 for CH4 oxidation to formaldehyde.\"\n\n[5] \"During CH4 oxidation to formaldehyde, the catalyst undergoes only a very small degree of reduction and typically only 50500 ppm of MoVI is reduced to MoIV.\"\n\n[6] \"It was established that treatment of MoOx/SiO2 at 873 K under pure methane reduces the dispersed molybdate species to only a limited extent and results mainly in the deposition of amorphous carbon.\"", "English": "The literature focuses on molybdenum oxide catalysts supported on silica (MoOx/SiO2) for methane oxidation to formaldehyde, rather than vanadium oxides or zeolites specifically. However, several insights can be drawn regarding the influence of composition, structure, and reaction conditions on the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations:\n\n1. Composition and structure: Isolated, pentacoordinated molybdate species containing a single Mo=O bond and supported on silica show the highest activity and selectivity for methane oxidation to formaldehyde. The isolated nature of these species contributes to their high specific activity.\n\n2. Reaction mechanism: The proposed mechanism involves the formation of peroxide species through the reaction of O2 with a small concentration of reduced molybdate species. These peroxides then react with methane to form formaldehyde. The catalyst undergoes very limited reduction during the reaction, with only 50-500 ppm of Mo(VI) reduced to Mo(IV), suggesting that the active oxygen species are not lattice oxygens.\n\n3. Reaction conditions: The catalyst is operated at high temperatures (873 K) and is influenced by the presence of water. Efficiency: The catalyst maintains a very low level of reduction during steady-state operation, contributing to its high efficiency. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Catalytic reactions of hydrocarbons in zeolites can be profoundly affected by extraframework transition-metal cationic clusters. The conversion passes a maximum at p of 0.3kPa. The main product remains propylene, although with increasing water content slightly increased amounts of methane and ethylene are formed.\"\n\n[5] \"The promoting effect of water is due to the formation of reactive partly hydrolyzed gallium species. For mononuclear gallium sites, the catalytic cycle is initiated by desorption of H2 from [Ga3+(H)(OH)]+ to form the GaO+ ion.\"\n\n[6] \"Dehydrogenation of an alkane over the Ga2O2 dimer proceeds by initial heterolytic dissociation by the Lewis acid pair formed by Ga3+ and the basic extraframework oxygen atom (Scheme1) with subsequent olefin desorption and hydrogen recombination.\"\n\n[7] \"In summary, addition of water to reduced Ga cations stabilizes binuclear hydroxyl-bridged Ga-containing cationic reaction intermediates. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The best results were obtained for a simple reaction, the oxidation of benzene to phenol over Fe-containing ZSM-5 zeolites. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Unpromoted HZSM-5 is, however, a poor dehydrogenation catalyst; addition of promoters is required for such application.\"\n\n[2] \"Modification of the zeolite with zinc or gallium has been successful for this purpose.\"\n\n[3] \"For the oxidative dehydrogenation of propane and n-butane, it has been reported that the alkene yield is highest over Fe3+ silicalite, and rapid cracking and combustion of propane occurred over ion-exchanged Fe/ZSM-5 and FeOx/silicalite.\"\n\n[4] \"Upon condensation of the vapor of a volatile precursor on the H-form of the zeolite, the concentration of Brnsted sites is lowered drastically and a high level of ion exchange is obtained. Subsequent treatment with H2O to remove chlorine from the precursor induces hydrolysis of the metal ions.\"\n\n[5] \"Hydrolysis converts naked ions into oxo ions, such as (GaO)+ and (HOFeOFeOH)2+. They are identified by temperature-programmed reduction with H2 and CO and, in the case of the binuclear Fe3+ ion, by ESR spectroscopy.\"\n\n[6] \"The Ga2O3 clusters are easily reduced to Ga+ at 450 C. With (HOFeOFeOH)2+ in cationic exchange positions reduction is reversible at 500 C.\"\n\n[7] \"In the case of Zn/ZSM-5, isolated Zn2+ cations compensate the charge of two Al-centered tetrahedra or attach themselves to one silanol group or ZnOH and one Al-centered tetrahedron. In this state, the Zn ions are stabilized and cannot be reduced below 800 C.\"\n\n[8] \"When Ga, Zn, and Fe replace protons in HZSM-5, they form strong Lewis acid sites.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly supported vanadium oxides and metal-exchanged zeolites, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in processes such as oxidative dehydrogenation and zeolite-catalyzed reactions.\n\nFor zeolite-catalyzed reactions, the addition of promoters like zinc or gallium to HZSM-5 improves its dehydrogenation catalytic activity. The method of introducing these metals, such as sublimation of volatile compounds followed by hydrolysis, affects the nature of the active sites. This process reduces Brønsted acid sites and creates strong Lewis acid sites, which can alter the catalyst's activity and selectivity.\n\nThe nature of the metal and its oxidation state play crucial roles in oxidative dehydrogenation. For instance, Fe3+ in silicalite shows high alkene yield for propane and n-butane dehydrogenation, while Fe/ZSM-5 promotes cracking and combustion. The structure of the metal species, such as isolated ions, oxo-species, or small clusters, influences the reaction pathway and product distribution.\n\nThe preparation method affects the final structure of the metal species in the zeolite. Hydrolysis can create oxo-ions like (GaO)+ and (HOFeOFeOH)2+, which have distinct catalytic properties. The reducibility of these species varies, with Ga2O3 clusters easily reduced at 450°C, (HOFeOFeOH)2+ undergoing reversible reduction at 500°C, and Zn2+ ions stable up to 800°C.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of metal-exchanged zeolites in alkane transformations. The ability to tune the catalyst's properties through metal selection, preparation method, and post-treatment allows for optimization of activity, selectivity, and stability for specific industrial processes. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Iron complexes in the ZSM-5 zeolite matrix (α-centers) are shown to perform single-turnover cycles of methane oxidation to methanol at room temperature when nitrous oxide is used as a source of oxygen.\"\n\n[2] \"FeZSM-5 zeolite containing iron complexes that form under thermal activation (called α-centers [7]) is able to perform single-turnover cycles of selective methane oxidation to methanol at room temperature when nitrous oxide (N2O) is the source of oxygen.\"\n\n[3] \"At temperatures lower than 573 K, N2O decomposition on α-centers quantitatively follows reaction (1): N2O + ( )α = (O)α + N2, loading the active centers with α-oxygen [7].\"\n\n[4] \"There are α-centers whose activity gives FeZSM-5 zeolites a unique ability to catalyze direct oxidation of benzene to phenol with nitrous oxide at 573-623 K, providing nearly 100 % selectivity [9,14].\"\n\n[5] \"Binuclear iron centers are a particular feature of MMO compared to the mononuclear centers of other monooxygenases [1]. {"Quotes": "[1] \"It has been found that, when propane is used as the reactant at 5OOC and 0.1 MPa, the BTX selectivity can be increased from ca. 10% (H-ZSM-5) to ca. 40 to 45% after treatment of the base zeolite with solutions of zinc or gallium nitrate, such that the final zinc or gallium content is ca. 1.0 mass-%.\"\n\n[2] \"On Zn-ZSM-5 part of the hydrogen atom pool lost on aromatization is released as dihydrogen and an improved BTX selectivity results.\"\n\n[3] \"It appears that Ga-ZSM-5 or GaZn-ZSM-5 catalysts operate in a similar manner, but gallium-containing samples are preferred since zinc volatilization occurs at the reaction temperatures used for samples containing zinc alone.\"\n\n[4] \"The contact time has been shown to have a strong influence on the product distribution obtained in these systems. To summarize, the observed selectivity to aromatics depends on the form of the zeolite used and on the contact time.\"\n\n[5] \"A comparative study of the conversion of propane, n-butane and i-butane over Zn-ZSM-5 reveals that the alkanes differ in terms of activity and BTX selectivity. i-Butane is the most reactive of the three alkanes and also yields the highest percentage hydrogen recovery as dihydrogen. However, it displays the lowest BTX selectivity.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in zeolite-catalyzed reactions such as the conversion of light alkanes to aromatics (BTX).\n\nComposition: Adding metals like zinc or gallium (around 1.0 mass-%) to H-ZSM-5 zeolites increases BTX selectivity from about 10% to 40-45% for propane conversion at 500°C and 0.1 MPa. Gallium-containing catalysts are preferred over zinc-containing ones due to zinc volatilization at high temperatures.\n\nStructure: ZSM-5 type zeolites are effective for this transformation. The metal component (Zn or Ga) is introduced by treating H-ZSM-5 with aqueous solutions of the respective metal nitrate.\n\nReaction conditions: Temperature (typically 500°C) and pressure (0.1 MPa) affect the process. Contact time strongly influences product distribution and aromatics selectivity.\n\nMechanism: On Zn-ZSM-5 and Ga-ZSM-5, part of the hydrogen lost during aromatization is released as dihydrogen, improving BTX selectivity. Different alkanes (propane, n-butane, i-butane) show varying activities and BTX selectivities.\n\nIndustrial significance: These catalysts allow for tunable selectivity and improved yields of desired aromatic products from light alkanes, which is important for upgrading lower-value hydrocarbons. The ability to convert light alkanes to more valuable aromatic compounds (BTX) is industrially important, making these processes more economically viable for industrial applications.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂的组成、结构和反应条件显著影响烷烃转化的机理和效率，特别是在沸石催化反应中，如轻烷烃转化为芳烃（BTX）的过程。\n\n组成：向H-ZSM-5沸石中添加锌或镓等金属（约1.0质量百分比）可以将丙烷转化的BTX选择性从约10%提高到40-45%（在500°C和0.1 MPa条件下）。由于锌在高温下易挥发，含镓催化剂比含锌催化剂更受青睐。\n\n结构：ZSM-5型沸石对这种转化很有效。金属组分（Zn或Ga）是通过用相应金属硝酸盐的水溶液处理H-ZSM-5引入的。\n\n反应条件：温度（通常为500°C）和压力（0.1 MPa）影响该过程。接触时间强烈影响产品分布和芳烃选择性。\n\n机理：在Zn-ZSM-5和Ga-ZSM-5上，芳构化过程中失去的部分氢以二氢的形式释放，改善了BTX选择性。不同的烷烃（丙烷、正丁烷、异丁烷）表现出不同的活性和BTX选择性。\n\n工业重要性：这些催化剂允许可调节的选择性，并从轻烷烃中获得所需芳香族产物的改进产率，这对于提升低价值烃类很重要。将轻烷烃转化为更有价值的芳烃化合物（BTX）的能力在工业上很重要，使这些过程在工业应用中更具经济可行性。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0166-9834(00)80384-x"},

In Zn/H-MFI catalysts, three types of zinc species are present: small and large ZnO clusters, and zinc cations. The specific form of zinc species depends on the zinc content, with high zinc content favoring the formation of (OZ)(ZnOZn)2+(OZ) or (ZO)Zn+OSi cations, although Zn2+ or ZnOH+ may also be present.\n\nThese zinc species, especially Zn2+ cations, act as strong Lewis sites and change the mechanism of alkane activation and transformation, favoring hydrogen removal. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The initial step in propane activation over Zn/H-MFI is dissociative adsorption over zinc oxide sites, leading to the formation of propyl zinc species and ZnOH groups.\"\n\n[2] \"At low partial pressure of the reactants, H2 recombinative desorption and hydrogen evolution is favoured, whereas at high pressures, implied under NMR batch conditions, the hydrogenolysis route is preferred.\"\n\n[3] \"The mechanism proposed for propane activation involves propane dissociation, followed by propene evolution and recombinative desorption of dihydrogen. {"Quotes": "[1] \"For supported metal oxides, it has been observed empirically that the decline in olefin selectivity with increasing alkane conversion decreases with increasing basicity of the support.\"\n\n[2] \"Figure 5 shows that the effects of the phosphorus/vanadium ratio on the selectivity of maleic anhydride formation via butane oxidation over supported vanadium phosphate catalysts.\"\n\n[3] \"The selectivity to maleic anhydride increases monotonically with increasing P/V (phosphorus/vanadium) ratio. For supported metal oxides, the basicity of the support affects olefin selectivity. As the support becomes more basic, the decline in olefin selectivity with increasing alkane conversion decreases.\n\n2. In vanadium phosphate catalysts, the phosphorus/vanadium (P/V) ratio plays a crucial role. The selectivity for maleic anhydride formation increases as the P/V ratio increases. This is linked to the stabilization of V in the 4+ oxidation state when P/V = 2.\n\n3. For supported vanadium oxide catalysts, the domain size of vanadia affects the rates of different reaction pathways in oxidative dehydrogenation (ODH). Larger vanadia domains are required for ODH reactions.\n\n4. For zeolite catalysts like Cu/ZSM-5 and Fe/ZSM-5, water vapor in the reaction environment affects their performance. While Cu/ZSM-5's activity is significantly suppressed by water vapor, Fe/ZSM-5 maintains high activity and selectivity even in its presence.\n\n5. Zeolite catalysts have specific operating constraints. They have low hydrothermal stability at high temperatures, narrow operating temperature windows, and their efficiency depends on the nature of the hydrocarbon reductant. They are also sensitive to sulfur poisoning.\n\n6. Hydrothermal degradation of zeolite catalysts is associated with dealumination and migration/agglomeration of metal ions and oxo complexes.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of these catalysts by affecting their selectivity, stability, and overall performance in alkane transformation processes. The ability to tune catalyst properties through composition and structure allows for optimization of industrial processes. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Modification of these zeolites with Zn2+ ions inhibits cracking and increases the rate and selectivity of aromatization.\"\n\n[2] \"It is generally believed that this is connected with acceleration by the modifying Zn2+ ions of dehydrogenation of both light paraffins and the growing chains of oligomers.\"\n\n[3] \"For spectral measurements, the granulated zeolites with particle dimensions of 0.51 mm were transferred into another part of the optical cell equipped with a CaF2 window.\"\n\n[4] \"Reaction with zinc vapor at 770 K resulted in almost complete disappearance of both the narrow and the broad bands (the dashed line in Figure 1).\"\n\n[5] \"Below 453 K such dissociative adsorption is irreversible, since the bands from the chemisorbed alkyl species and protons were not removed, even by a very prolonged evacuation.\"\n\n[6] \"The resulting ethylene is most likely involved in a subsequent reaction with acidic protons yielding the grafted oligomeric species that, after heating of the sample at high temperature, contributes to the DRIFT spectrum in the region of CH stretching vibrations.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly zinc-modified zeolites, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations. Key findings include:\n\n1. Composition: Modification of zeolites with Zn2+ ions inhibits cracking and increases the rate and selectivity of aromatization. Zinc can be incorporated through wet ion exchange or reaction with zinc vapor, with vapor deposition resulting in higher zinc content.\n\n2. {"Quotes": "\"The high temperature oxidation of CH4 to HCHO may be carried out over pure SiO2 and V2O5/SiO5. In the single-pass mode, the HCHO yields do not exceed 34%; however, respectable spacetime-yields (STY) of about 1200 g/kg cat h at 30% selectivity have been achieved over a 2% V2O5/SiO2 catalyst at 600C [20].\"\n\n\"Several bifunctional catalysts are known to promote this reaction, with the most thoroughly studied being a Mo/H-ZSM-5 zeolite [3538].\"\n\n\"Most investigators agree that molybdenum carbide or oxycarbide is responsible for the conversion of CH4 to C2H4 and that the C2H4 is converted to aromatic products over the acidic sites within the channels of the zeolite.\"\n\n\"A W, Zn/H-ZSM-5 catalyst, prepared by Zhang and co-workers [38] via a controlled impregnation technique, is of particular interest because a CH4 conversion of 23% at 850C, with high benzene selectivity, has been observed.\"\n\n\"Over the better catalysts, which include SrO/La2O3 [25] and Mn/Na2WO4/SiO2 [26,27], a C2 selectivity of about 80% can be achieved at a CH4 conversion of 20%.\"\n\n\"Other metals including W and Fe are effective for promoting this reaction, and there is evidence that these metals are active as suboxides, rather than as carbides [37].\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in processes like oxidative dehydrogenation and zeolite-catalyzed reactions:\n\n1. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Oxidative dehydrogenation of alkanes provides a thermodynamically accessible route to the synthesis of alkenes from alkanes (13). Supported vanadium oxides (VOx) catalyze this reaction, but unselective combustion pathways limit alkene selectivities, especially at high conversions (418).\"\n\n[2] \"The extent of dispersion and the local and extended structure of supported VOx species depend on the chemical identity and the surface area of the support (13, 17, 18).\"\n\n[3] \"Polyvanadate species that form on ZrO2 at VOx surface densities above 34 VOx/nm2 provide active and selective sites for oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. Catalysts with lower VOx surface density and uncovered ZrO2 surfaces show lower alkene selectivities because of competing oxidation pathways leading to undesired CO and CO2 products.\"\n\n[4] \"Initial propene selectivities increase with increasing VOx surface density, as monovanadate species and exposed support sites, which favor primary combustion pathways, decrease in concentration.\"\n\n[5] \"Oxidative dehydrogenation rates per V-atom reach a maximum on VOx domains of intermediate size, which provide a balance between the activity of surface VOx species and their accessibility to reactants.\"\n\n[6] \"Interactions with supports determine the type of VOx structures present at a given surface density, but turnover rates do not depend on the identity of the support when differences in VOx structure are taken into account.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of supported vanadium oxide catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in oxidative dehydrogenation processes. Key factors include:\n\n1. Catalyst composition: The type of support (e.g., ZrO2, Al2O3, SiO2) and vanadium loading affect the dispersion and structure of VOx species.\n\n2. VOx surface density: Higher surface densities generally lead to the formation of polyvanadate species, which are more active and selective for oxidative dehydrogenation. Optimal rates occur at intermediate densities that balance activity and reactant accessibility.\n\n3. Support interactions: The chemical identity of the support influences the dispersion and structure of VOx species at a given surface density. However, turnover rates do not depend on the support identity when VOx structural differences are accounted for.\n\n4. VOx structure: The evolution from isolated monovanadates to polyvanadate domains affects catalytic behavior. Polyvanadate species are generally more selective for alkene formation.\n\n5. Reaction conditions: High conversions can lead to unselective combustion pathways, limiting alkene selectivity.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of supported vanadium oxide catalysts by:\n\n1. Allowing tuning of catalyst properties to optimize alkene yield and selectivity.\n2. Providing a means to balance the competing requirements of activity and selectivity.\n3. Enabling control of VOx structure and dispersion through support selection and surface density manipulation.\n\nHowever, challenges remain in maximizing alkene yields, particularly at high conversions, due to competing combustion reactions. The study does not directly address metal-exchanged zeolites or their specific industrial significance in alkane transformations.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂的组成、结构和反应条件，特别是负载型钒氧化物催化剂，显著影响烷烃转化的机理和效率，尤其是在氧化脱氢过程中。关键因素包括：\n\n1. 催化剂组成：载体类型（如ZrO2、Al2O3、SiO2）和钒负载量影响VOx物种的分散和结构。\n\n2. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Zeolites are crystalline alumosilicates and as such are of no interest for redox reactions. Unlike other oxides, they have an intracrystalline system of micropores of molecular dimensions. Chemical composition of zeolites can be modified by transition metals due to their incorporation either into the crystal lattice or into the micropore space.\"\n\n[2] \"Modification with Fe is a special case. Unlike other metals, whose oxides initially exhibit some activity of the same sort as that after the introduction into the zeolite, iron atoms in ZSM-5 matrix acquire fundamentally new features compared to the free Fe2O3.\"\n\n[3] \"The iron loses its ability to activate O2, but acquires special affinity towards nitrous oxide, causing its decomposition in a particular way [53]. This reaction gives rise to the formation of a new form of surface oxygen (called a-oxygen [54]) which, as one can see further, is behind a unique performance of FeZSM-5 zeolites in the oxidation with N2O.\"\n\n[4] \"The study of parafn partial oxidation catalysts gave different observations [44]. In this case, to avoid overoxidation, the active sites (usually vanadium ions) must be isolated in the inert matrix of the support to prevent oxygen diffusion from the neighboring sites.\"\n\n[5] \"A detailed study of vanadium oxide supported on a variety of carriers [45] concluded that the presence of VOV fragments was essential for the selective oxidation.\"\n\n[6] \"Bulk oxides with the oxygen of low lability (MgO, ZnO, TiO2, etc.), or silica-supported oxides of V, Mo, W are usually used for this purpose.\"\n\n[7] \"The distribution of iron and other metals in zeolites has been studied extensively. In general, Fe can occupy three positions in ZSM-5 matrix [8487] and can exist as:\n1. Isolated ions in tetrahedral positions of the crystal lattice;\n2. Isolated ions or small complexes inside the intracrystalline micropore space;\n3. Finely dispersed oxide phase on the outer surface of zeolite crystals.\"\n\n[8] \"Depending on Fe content and on the mode of catalyst activation, Ca can be regulated within several orders of magnitude, reaching up to nearly 100 mmol/g for the most active catalysts.\"\n\n[9] \"Experimentally, observed characteristics of a-oxygen can be explained by binuclear quantum chemical model of a-sites [92].\"\n\n[10] \"According to recent quantum mechanical calculations [99], methane oxidation on FeZSM-5 proceeds with participation of binuclear complexes having Fe atoms bound by (m-oxo-) and (m-hydroxo-) bridges.\"\n\n[11] \"Recently, based on successful pilot plant operation, Solutia made an announcement of the jointly developed new process and shared its plans for fast-track commercialization [113]. {"Quotes": "[1] \"The zinc-exchanged (ZSM-5-Zn) and proton-exchanged (ZSM-5-H) forms of ZSM-5 zeolite have been studied for the conversion of propane to aromatic hydrocarbons at temperatures in the range 730-820 K.\"\n\n[2] \"ZSM-5-Zn was the more active and gave the better BTX selectivity (60-7OC%).\"\n\n[3] \"The main features of the conversion mechanism are proposed involving propane dehydrogenation, followed by oligomerization and aromatization.\"\n\n[4] \"The primary dehydrogenation reaction is mechanistically different on the two types of catalyst: over ZSM-5-H dehydrogenation is rate controlled, while over ZSM-5-Zn this step is in quasi-equilibrium.\"\n\n[5] \"We suggest that this effect arises because the respective dehydrogenation steps are in quasi-equilibrium, with reaction 4 controlling the conversion and a dehydrogenation between aromatic and cyclic precursor controlling the BTX selectivity (both processes may well involve species of the type [Zn-H]+, c.f. reaction 4.\"\n\n[6] \"In the case of the ZSM-5-Zn catalyst, we suggest the zinc cation acts as a hydride acceptor to give a transient species such as [Zn-HI+ (and thence hydrogen)\"\n\n[7] \"Over both ZSM-5-H and ZSM-5-Zn catalysts, ethane reactant was found to be much less reactive than propane: at 870 K the extent of ethane conversion was < 5%.\"\n\n[8] \"With both catalysts, as expected, the propane conversion fell with increasing space velocity but the product distributions behaved differently.\"\n\n[9] \"The apparent activation energies, obtained from Arrhenius plots of the propane conversions, were ZSM-5-Zn (I.28 wt% aluminium), 121+15 kJ mol-'; ZSM-5-Zn (0.71 wt% aluminium), 104+15 kJ mol-'; ZSM-5-H (1.28 wt% aluminium), 120t15 kJ mol-'.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations, particularly in zeolite-catalyzed reactions. Key findings include:\n\n1. Catalyst composition: Zinc-exchanged ZSM-5 (ZSM-5-Zn) shows higher activity and better BTX (benzene, toluene, xylene) selectivity compared to proton-exchanged ZSM-5 (ZSM-5-H). The zinc cation acts as a hydride acceptor, forming transient [Zn-H]+ species.\n\n2. Reaction mechanism: The process involves propane dehydrogenation, followed by oligomerization and aromatization. The primary dehydrogenation step differs mechanistically between ZSM-5-H (rate-controlled) and ZSM-5-Zn (quasi-equilibrium).\n\n3. Reaction conditions:\n   - Temperature: Efficient conversion occurs in the range of 730-820 K.\n   - Space velocity: Increasing space velocity decreases propane conversion but affects product distribution differently for each catalyst.\n   - Reactant type: Propane is much more reactive than ethane under similar conditions.\n\n4. Activation energy: Similar for both catalysts (around 120 kJ/mol), suggesting a similar overall reaction mechanism despite differences in the rate-determining step.\n\n5. Equilibrium considerations: In ZSM-5-Zn, dehydrogenation steps are in quasi-equilibrium, controlling both conversion and BTX selectivity through [Zn-H]+ species.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of metal-exchanged zeolites, particularly ZSM-5-Zn, in alkane transformation processes. The higher activity and better BTX selectivity of ZSM-5-Zn make it a promising catalyst for the production of valuable aromatic compounds from propane, which is an important industrial process. Understanding these factors can guide the development of more efficient catalysts for industrial applications in petrochemical processes.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂的组成、结构和反应条件显著影响烷烃转化的机理和效率，特别是在沸石催化反应中。主要发现包括：\n\n1. 催化剂组成：锌交换型ZSM-5（ZSM-5-Zn）比质子交换型ZSM-5（ZSM-5-H）表现出更高的活性和更好的BTX（苯、甲苯、二甲苯）选择性。锌阳离子作为氢化物接受体，形成瞬态[Zn-H]+物种。\n\n2. 反应机理：过程涉及丙烷脱氢，随后进行寡聚和芳构化。主要脱氢步骤在ZSM-5-H（速率控制）和ZSM-5-Zn（准平衡）之间在机理上有所不同。\n\n3. 反应条件：\n   - 温度：在730-820 K范围内进行高效转化。\n   - 空速：增加空速会降低丙烷转化率，但对每种催化剂的产物分布影响不同。\n   - 反应物类型：在相似条件下，丙烷比乙烷更具反应性。\n\n4. 活化能：两种催化剂相似（约120 kJ/mol），表明尽管速率决定步骤不同，但总体反应机理相似。\n\n5. 平衡考虑：在ZSM-5-Zn中，脱氢步骤处于准平衡状态，通过[Zn-H]+物种控制转化率和BTX选择性。\n\n这些因素促进了金属交换沸石，特别是ZSM-5-Zn，在烷烃转化过程中的工业重要性。ZSM-5-Zn的更高活性和更好的BTX选择性使其成为从丙烷生产有价值芳烃化合物的有前景的催化剂，这是一个重要的工业过程。理解这些因素可以指导开发更高效的催化剂，用于石油化工过程中的工业应用。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0166-9834(00)82709-8"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"Additional evidence is presented for the role of gallium reduction in preparing active Ga/ZSM-5 catalysts for alkane aromatization.\"\n\n[2] \"Although reduction generates dispersed, active gallium species in zeolite channels, it is shown that for ethane dehydrogenation to aromatics the reduced (with hydrogen) Ga/ZSM-5 catalysts are not as active or selective as are materials which have been substantially reoxidized either by air or by traces of oxygen in inert gases.\"\n\n[3] \"Optimal catalysts for ethane aromatization are prepared by reduction with hydrogen to disperse the gallium, followed by reoxidation to a dispersed Ga3+ phase.\"\n\n[4] \"A substantially reduced catalyst (Ga+/Z- ca. 1) is both less active and selective for aromatics formation. Such catalysts also show lower hydrocracking activities than either unreduced or reoxidized materials, because of the reduction in Brønsted acidity associated with the transformation to Ga+Z- sites.\"\n\n[5] \"It is generally agreed that the primary role of extra-framework gallium in these materials is to enhance rates of alkene, diene, or cycloalkene dehydrogenation\"\n\n[6] \"We propose that at the higher drying temperature used here (650 C) a small amount of Ga2O3 was reduced prior to the introduction of hydrogen, in agreement with the chemistry of bulk Ga2O3 at > 600 C\"\n\n[7] \"The activity and aromatics selectivity for the series of Ga/HMFI catalysts generally followed the order B (reduced/oxidized) > C (reduced/He) > A (reduced) > D (reduced/oxidized/reduced).\"\n\n[8] \"A combination of thermogravimetric analysis (TGA), differential scanning calorimetry (DSC), and X-ray diffraction (XRD) studies has been used to confirm that rapid reoxidation takes place at 550C. However, the reoxidation does not regenerate β-Ga2O3, but rather a higher energy, dispersed Ga3+ which appears to be optimal for production of aromatics from ethane.\"\n\n[9] \"Reoxidized catalysts are stable under the reaction conditions used here (530-570°C, low hydrocarbon partial pressures), but are not stable to re-reduction by hydrogen at higher partial pressures.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly Ga/ZSM-5, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in processes like aromatization and dehydrogenation. Key factors include:\n\n1. Gallium reduction and reoxidation: The reduction of gallium is crucial for dispersing active species within zeolite channels. However, optimal catalysts are prepared by reduction followed by partial reoxidation, forming dispersed Ga3+ phases.\n\n2. Oxidation state: The balance between Ga3+ and Ga+ species affects catalyst performance. Fully reduced catalysts (Ga+/Z- ≈ 1) show lower activity and selectivity for aromatics formation and decreased hydrocracking activity due to reduced Brønsted acidity.\n\n3. Preparation method: The sequence of reduction and oxidation treatments significantly impacts catalyst performance. Catalysts reduced then oxidized generally show higher activity and selectivity than those only reduced or subjected to multiple reduction-oxidation cycles.\n\n4. Temperature effects: High drying temperatures (e.g., 650°C) can lead to partial reduction of Ga2O3 even before hydrogen introduction. Reoxidation at 550°C produces a high-energy, dispersed Ga3+ phase optimal for ethane aromatization.\n\n5. Reaction conditions: Catalyst stability depends on temperature and gas composition. Reoxidized catalysts are stable at 530-570°C with low hydrocarbon partial pressures but can be re-reduced at higher hydrogen partial pressures.\n\n6. Extra-framework gallium: It enhances rates of alkene, diene, or cycloalkene dehydrogenation, contributing to overall catalyst performance.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of Ga/ZSM-5 catalysts by allowing fine-tuning of catalyst properties to optimize specific reactions, such as alkane aromatization, and improve overall process efficiency.", "Chinese": "金属基催化剂，特别是Ga/ZSM-5的组成、结构和反应条件显著影响烷烃转化过程（如芳构化和脱氢）的机理和效率。关键因素包括：\n\n1. 镓的还原和再氧化：镓的还原对于在沸石通道内分散活性物种至关重要。然而，最佳催化剂是通过还原后部分再氧化制备的，形成分散的Ga3+相。\n\n2. 氧化态：Ga3+和Ga+物种之间的平衡影响催化剂性能。完全还原的催化剂（Ga+/Z- ≈ 1）由于布朗斯特酸性降低，表现出较低的芳烃形成活性和选择性，以及降低的加氢裂化活性。\n\n3. 制备方法：还原和氧化处理的顺序显著影响催化剂性能。先还原后氧化的催化剂通常比仅还原或经过多次还原-氧化循环的催化剂表现出更高的活性和选择性。\n\n4. 温度效应：高干燥温度（如650°C）可导致Ga2O3在引入氢气之前就部分还原。在550°C下再氧化产生一种高能量、分散的Ga3+相，这对乙烷芳构化最为理想。\n\n5. 反应条件：催化剂稳定性取决于温度和气体组成。再氧化的催化剂在530-570°C和低烃类分压下稳定，但在较高的氢气分压下可能被再次还原。\n\n6. 骨架外镓：它提高烯烃、二烯烃或环烯烃的脱氢速率，有助于整体催化剂性能。\n\n这些因素通过允许对催化剂性能进行微调以优化特定反应（如烷烃芳构化）并提高整体过程效率，从而提高了Ga/ZSM-5催化剂的工业重要性。", "Doi": "10.1016/0926-860x(92)80336-b"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Generally, zeolite protonic acidity is necessary for NO reduction: In contrast to H,Ga-ZSM-5, Na,Ga-ZSM-5 was inactive. The authors concluded that a synergism does exist between Ga species and H+ enabling the catalyst to activate the reductant (methane) for NO decomposition in the presence of O2.\"\n\n[2] \"Ga-modified ZSM-5 is far better than the Cu-modified version, which is even less active than unmodified ZSM-5. This indicates that the reaction can be accomplished to a considerable extent in the absence of any metal-related redox centers.\"\n\n[3] \"Framework gallium in an isolated tetrahedral environment cannot be reduced at moderate temperatures. The observed reducibility of gallium-modified zeolites therefore indicates the presence of nonframework gallium species.\"\n\n[4] \"Aromatization of liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) alkanes into aromatic components (mainly benzene, toluene, and xylenes, BTX) on Ga-modified ZSM-5 catalysts is commercialized in the Cyclar process jointly developed by UOP and BP.\"\n\n[5] \"Isomorphous substitution and replacement of exchangeable cations are important ways to modify zeolite properties for practical applications and have achieved considerable interest in the field of zeolite chemistry.\"\n\n[6] \"The chemical shift, δ, of a 29Si nucleus in a zeolite depends primarily on the number of T atoms in the first neighboring shell and on the TOT angles (T = tetrahedral species, Si, Al, Ga, Fe, Ge, etc.) of the bridging oxygen atoms that coordinate the 29Si nucleus.\"\n\n[7] \"Brnsted acidity within silicate-like materials is generated when tetravalent Si4+ is replaced with trivalent ions such as Al3+ or Ga3+.\"\n\n[8] \"Nonframework gallium is the source of Lewis acidity. Oxo cations GaO+ on exchange positions of the framework behave as Lewis acids.\"\n\n[9] \"Characteristically, IR vibration bands in both the hydroxyl region (wavenumbers beyond 3000 cm-1) and the framework region (wavenumbers below 1500 cm-1) are sensitive to the composition of the framework.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly supported vanadium oxides and metal-exchanged zeolites, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations. Key factors include:\n\n1. Composition:\n- Isomorphous substitution of Si by trivalent ions like Ga3+ or Al3+ in zeolites generates Brønsted acidity.\n- The presence of framework and non-framework metal species affects catalyst acidity and activity.\n- Non-framework gallium species contribute to Lewis acidity.\n\n2. Structure:\n- The zeolite framework structure influences catalytic properties, with factors like T-O-T angles affecting 29Si NMR chemical shifts.\n- Unit cell dimensions and IR vibration bands are sensitive to framework composition.\n- Shape-selective properties of zeolites can optimize product selectivities in various reactions.\n\n3. Reaction conditions:\n- Temperature affects the reducibility of metal species, with framework gallium being non-reducible at moderate temperatures.\n- The presence of oxygen can influence reaction pathways, as seen in NO decomposition using methane as a reductant.\n\n4. Synergistic effects:\n- A synergism between Ga species and H+ enables methane activation for NO decomposition.\n- The combination of Brønsted and Lewis acidity from framework and non-framework species contributes to overall catalyst performance.\n\n5. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Ga and Zn species increase the rates of propane chemical conversion, recombinative hydrogen desorption, and deuterium incorporation from D2 into reaction products.\"\n\n[2] \"Disposal of hydrogen formed in C-H bond activation steps occurs by transfer of H-atoms to unsaturated species to form alkanes or to Ga and Zn species, which catalyze the recombinative desorption of H-atoms to form dihydrogen (H2).\"\n\n[3] \"In-situ X-ray absorption studies suggest that Ga and Zn species reside at cation exchange sites as monomeric cations and that recombinative desorption involve reduction-oxidation cycles of such cations during each dehydrocyclodimerization turnover.\"\n\n[4] \"The addition of metal cations also increases the deuterium content in 'unreacted' propane (Fig. 18). The rate of incorporation of D-atoms into 'unreacted' propane provides an independent measure of the D-content in the surface pool\"\n\n[5] \"Clearly, Ga and Zn species increase the reversibility of H-atom recombinative desorption steps and act as efficient 'portholes' for the removal of H-atoms produced during C-H bond activation steps.\"\n\n[6] \"The rate of propane dehydrocyclodimerization to form C6+ aromatics is limited by a sequence of irreversible dehydrogenation reactions leading to propene, higher alkenes, dienes, trienes, and aromatics.\"\n\n[7] \"Ga and Zn ions increase the rate of removal of alkenes from these oligomerization-cracking cycles. This removal must occur by the formation of products, such as aromatics (and H2) and alkanes, which are much less reactive than alkenes in acid-catalyzed reactions.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly metal-exchanged zeolites like Ga/H-ZSM5 and Zn/H-ZSM5, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in processes such as oxidative dehydrogenation and zeolite-catalyzed reactions.\n\nComposition: The addition of Ga and Zn to H-ZSM5 increases the rates of propane chemical conversion, recombinative hydrogen desorption, and deuterium incorporation from D2 into reaction products. These metal species act as efficient \"portholes\" for the removal of H-atoms produced during C-H bond activation steps.\n\nStructure: In-situ X-ray absorption studies show that Ga and Zn species reside at cation exchange sites as monomeric cations within the zeolite structure. This positioning allows them to effectively catalyze the recombinative desorption of H-atoms to form dihydrogen (H2).\n\nReaction mechanism: The metal cations undergo reduction-oxidation cycles during each dehydrocyclodimerization turnover. They increase the reversibility of H-atom recombinative desorption steps and enhance the rate of removal of alkenes from oligomerization-cracking cycles, promoting the formation of more stable products like aromatics and H2.\n\nReaction conditions: The presence of deuterium in isotope studies reveals the mechanism of these catalysts. The incorporation of deuterium into reaction products and unreacted propane demonstrates the reversibility of hydrogen adsorption/desorption steps on metal-modified zeolites.\n\nEfficiency: The presence of Ga and Zn increases the overall efficiency of alkane transformations by providing an alternate pathway for hydrogen disposal. This prevents unwanted side reactions and increases the selectivity towards desired products.\n\nThese factors contribute to the industrial significance of metal-exchanged zeolites in alkane transformation processes. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Application of alternative oxidants in the form of various oxygen-containing molecules opens new possibilities. The idea of this approach is as follows. For supported vanadium oxides, the use of alternative oxidants like N2O can change the state of surface oxygen, allowing better control of selectivity compared to traditional O2 oxidation. This was demonstrated in the oxidation of benzene using vanadia catalysts, where N2O achieved much higher selectivity than O2 at 550°C.\n\nFor metal-exchanged zeolites, particularly iron-containing ones, the catalytic activity stems from either the acidic nature of zeolites (Brønsted and Lewis sites) or the presence of transition metal admixtures. The iron forms specific active sites called α-sites within the zeolite structure, which are responsible for the selective transfer of oxygen atoms from N2O to hydrocarbon molecules. The reaction mechanism involves a reversible redox transition between Fe2+ and Fe3+ states, occurring at elevated temperatures (over 200°C) in the presence of N2O.\n\nReaction conditions, especially temperature, play a crucial role in determining efficiency and selectivity. At elevated temperatures, N2O can be used for oxidative dehydrogenation of alkanes and epoxidation reactions with good selectivities. However, high temperatures can also lead to side reactions and coking, causing catalyst deactivation.\n\nThe industrial significance of these catalysts is influenced by their selectivity, efficiency, and stability. {"Quotes": "[1] \"It has been demonstrated that the nature and the dispersion of the metal oxide phase have a great inuence on the catalysts behavior.\"\n\n          [2] \"Likewise, Irusta et al. Key factors include:\n\n          1. Composition and structure: For supported vanadium oxides, the presence of terminal oxygen sites (V=O) is crucial for selective oxidation to oxygenates, while species without these sites lead to complete oxidation. In W/HZSM-5 catalysts, three types of tungsten species exist: isolated tetrahedral species, octahedral polymeric species, and WO3 crystallites. Their relative amounts change with tungsten loading, affecting catalyst performance.\n\n          2. Metal loading and dispersion: Metal loading influences the dispersion of the metal oxide phase, which in turn affects selectivity. For example, formaldehyde selectivity in W/HZSM-5 catalysts is related to the dispersion of the tungsten oxide phase. Higher loading can lead to increased polytungstate species, decreased dispersion, and partial blocking of zeolite pores.\n\n          3. Active sites: Both active oxygen ions and Brønsted acidic sites on HZSM-5 are active centers for methane activation. {"Quotes": "[1] \"We report here that a zirconium hydride complex, grafted onto the surface of silica, acquires such high electrophilic properties, that the reaction of o-bond metathesis between the Zr hydride and the C-H bonds of cyclooctane and methane becomes feasible.\"\n\n          [2] \"The silica surface enhances the electrophilicity of the zirconium centre, allowing the reaction of C-H activation of alkanes.\"\n\n          [3] \"This increase in the electrophilic character of the metal is probably related to the stabilization of an 8e-Zr by the surface siloxy ligands, while molecular analogues are usually stabilized by two cyclopentadienyl ligands and thus have a 16e-configuration.\"\n\n          [4] \"A common feature of these complexes is that the metal is in its highest oxidation state; it therefore, has a do electron configuration and is consequently highly electrophilic.\"", "English": "The literature focuses on a silica-supported zirconium hydride catalyst for alkane transformations, rather than vanadium oxides or metal-exchanged zeolites. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Gallium-containing ZSM-5 formulations are industrially preferred mainly due to the high volatility of zinc, and our discussion below describes the synthesis and catalytic function of these Ga-based formulations.\"\n\n[2] \"The aromatization of liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) alkanes to aromatics (mainly benzene, toluene, and xylenes, BTX) on Ga-modified ZSM-5 catalysts is commercialized in the Cyclar process jointly developed by UOP and BP.\"\n\n[3] \"Ga3 cations, in the as-prepared catalysts, irrespective of the preparation technique, are re-dispersed under the strongly reducing conditions and high temperatures prevalent during aromatization resulting in the active formulation of the catalyst.\"\n\n[4] \"Wet impregnation of HZSM-5 with gallium salt solutions (Gallium nitrate in general) guarantees gallium deposition on the catalyst, nevertheless, most of the gallium is found to be located on the outside of the zeolite crystals as evidenced by XPS and electron microscopy studies.\"\n\n[5] \"The gallium sites were considered to participate in alkane activation by dehydrogenation to form alkenes and hydrogenolysis to generate methane, adsorption/desorption of unsaturated compounds, dehydrogenation of olefinic compounds to give dienes and dehydrogenation of napthenic compounds to aromatics.\"\n\n[6] \"Based on setting the gallium parameters to be zero, the authors were also able to comment on the relative importance of gallium sites for various mechanisms.
