{"Quotes": "[1] \"We examine possible reaction mechanisms for the oxidative dehydrogenation of propane by supported transition metal oxide catalysts. Specifically we are interested in V2O5 supported on SiO22,12,13 and consider monomeric OV(O)3 surface species, which together with dimeric and oligomeric V2O5 species are present on catalyst surfaces with low V2O5 loadings.\"\n\n[2] \"Hydrogen abstraction by the vanadyl oxygen atom is the initial step in the oxidative dehydrogenation of propane by supported vanadium oxide species. The diradical intermediate that is reached via the diradicaloid transition structure Ts1 consists of a propyl radical attached to a HOV(O)3 site and has similar energies in the singlet and triplet states (Int2).\"\n\n[3] \"For V2O5/SiO2 catalysts with vanadium surface coverages below 3 V/nm2 (i.e., below the limit at which V2O5 crystallites start to appear) turnover frequencies (TOF) of around 0.01 s-1 (748 K) 37 and 0.3 × 10-3 s-1 (623 K) 38 have been observed for propene formation.\"\n\n[4] \"Comparison with recent DFT calculations for V2O5(001) crystal surfaces9 indicates that vanadia sites may be significantly more active in the ODH of propane if they are part of the bulk surface and not supported as monomers on silica. However, apparent turnover frequencies may be lower for V2O5 crystallites on the surface because only a fraction of sites is accessible in three-dimensional particles.\"\n\n[5] \"The initial step is hydrogen abstraction from propane by the vanadyl oxygen atom leading to a diradical intermediate, namely, C3H7•·HOVIV(O)3.\"\n\n[6] \"We analyzed possible reaction mechanisms for the oxidative dehydrogenation of propane by monomeric vanadium oxide species on silica.\"\n\n[7] \"Desorption of propyl radicals leads to a stationary concentration of propyl in the gas phase and leaves reduced HOVIV(O)3 sites on the surface. Due to fast reoxidation their concentration is much smaller than the concentration of OVV sites (Int0).\"\n\n[8] \"We investigate possible mechanisms of oxidative dehydrogenation of propane using density functional theory. Monomeric vanadium oxide species supported on silica are modeled by vanadyl-substituted silsesquioxane.\"\n\n[9] \"The initial CH bond activation step is hydrogen abstraction by the vanadyl (OVV) group yielding a diradical intermediate in which a propyl radical is bound to a HOVIV site.\"\n\n[10] \"We predict that at 750 K the apparent activation energy is 123  5 kJ/mol and the rate constant is about 0.26 s-1, in close agreement with experiments.\"\n\n[11] \"The first hydrogen abstraction occurs exclusively on OVV sites, while the second hydrogen abstraction can also occur on VOSi bridging oxygen sites.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts, particularly supported vanadium oxides, significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations in oxidative dehydrogenation (ODH) processes.\n\nComposition and Structure:\n1. The catalysts consist of V2O5 supported on SiO2, with monomeric OV(O)3 surface species, along with dimeric and oligomeric V2O5 species at low V2O5 loadings.\n2. The vanadium surface coverage is crucial, with optimal activity observed below 3 V/nm2, before V2O5 crystallites start to form.\n3. The active sites are modeled as vanadyl-substituted silsesquioxane, representing monomeric vanadium oxide species on silica.\n\nReaction Mechanism:\n1. The initial step involves hydrogen abstraction by the vanadyl (OVV) oxygen atom, forming a diradical intermediate (C3H7•·HOVIV(O)3).\n2. The first hydrogen abstraction occurs exclusively on OVV sites, while the second can also happen on VOSi bridging oxygen sites.\n3. Desorption of propyl radicals leads to a stationary concentration in the gas phase and leaves reduced HOVIV sites on the surface.\n4. Fast reoxidation maintains a low concentration of reduced sites compared to OVV sites.\n\nReaction Conditions and Efficiency:\n1. Temperature significantly affects the reaction kinetics. At 750 K, the apparent activation energy is predicted to be 123 ± 5 kJ/mol, with a rate constant of about 0.26 s-1.\n2. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Several different compounds, particularly silica supported metal oxides [1,2] were used in the process. Recently it has been mentioned that ZSM-5 [3] and ZSM-5 combined with molybdenum [4,5] or tungsten [6] were investigated. Silica supported V2O5 and MoO3 were used most frequently. They are considered to be the most effective in the production of formaldehyde [7,8].\"\n\n[2] \"Fe-ZSM-5 was used as a catalyst for the room temperature methane oxidation by N2O [1317]. The activation of methane over Fe-ZSM-5 is believed to be similar to methane activation in MMO thus to employ a redox mechanism.\"\n\n[3] \"The reaction was carried out at the atmospheric pressure at 350650 8C. ZSM-5 molecular sieves with the iron and silicon tetrahedral framework were used as catalysts. The Si/Fe molar ratio was 45, 34 and 22. Fe-ZSM-5 was applied both in the sodium and hydrogen form.\"\n\n[4] \"Higher values of methane conversion were acquired when Fe-HZSM-5 (31.51% for Si/Fe = 22) was used. Fe-NaZSM-5 resulted in procuring higher values of the selectivity of the oxidation of methane to methanol (74% for Si/Fe = 45).\"\n\n[5] \"It was found that increasing the temperature as well as extending the contact time increases the conversion of methane to methanol and at the same time lowers the value of the selectivity of the oxidation of methane to methanol.\"\n\n[6] \"Increasing the iron content resulted in the rise of methane conversion. The selectivity of the oxidation of methane to oxygenates displayed a slight grow along with the drop of the iron content, while the selectivity of methane oxidation to carbon dioxide was falling.\"", "English": "The composition, structure, and reaction conditions of metal-based catalysts significantly influence the mechanisms and efficiency of alkane transformations:\n\n1. Catalyst composition: Various metal-based catalysts are used, including silica-supported metal oxides (V2O5, MoO3), metal-exchanged zeolites (Fe-ZSM-5), and ZSM-5 combined with molybdenum or tungsten. Silica-supported V2O5 and MoO3 are considered most effective for formaldehyde production.\n\n2. Catalyst structure: ZSM-5 molecular sieves with iron and silicon in the tetrahedral framework are used, with varying Si/Fe molar ratios (45, 34, 22). The catalyst can be in sodium (Fe-NaZSM-5) or hydrogen (Fe-HZSM-5) form, affecting its performance.\n\n3. Metal content: For Fe-ZSM-5 catalysts, increasing iron content (lower Si/Fe ratio) leads to higher methane conversion but lower selectivity to oxygenates and higher selectivity to carbon dioxide.\n\n4. Reaction conditions: \n   - Temperature: Reactions are typically carried out at 350-650°C. Higher temperatures increase methane conversion but decrease selectivity to methanol.\n   - Pressure: Atmospheric pressure is used.\n   - Contact time: Longer contact times increase methane conversion but decrease selectivity to methanol.\n\n5. Reaction mechanism: The activation of methane over Fe-ZSM-5 is believed to follow a redox mechanism similar to methane monooxygenase (MMO) in biological systems.\n\nThese factors contribute to industrial significance by allowing control over product distribution and reaction efficiency.
